## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (concentration–time rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time derivative of a reactant concentration A, so the task is to infer an ordinary differential equation (rate law) from concentration–time data. With only t and A available, plausible models are zero/first/nth-order decay, self-limiting or autocatalytic terms, and explicit time-dependent rate coefficients (e.g., catalyst deactivation or programmed feeds).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption when A is abundant or surface-limited)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay / pseudo-first-order consumption)
- Nth-order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical order for elementary/overall rate behavior)
- General polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (lumped kinetics / Taylor-like local approximation)
- Autocatalytic growth term: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (self-accelerating production of A in autocatalysis)
- Logistic-type self-limiting formation: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (growth with carrying-capacity-like inhibition, e.g., limited precursor)
- Reversible-like relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (first-order return toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Time-varying first-order (catalyst deactivation/programmed conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate coefficient changes exponentially in time)
- Aging/activation with saturating time factor: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps from 0 to steady value as conditions establish)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., pulsed illumination or mixing): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-modulated pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Linear time drift in rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (slow drift in effective rate constant)
- Rational inhibition by A (self-inhibition without extra species): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective saturation/inhibition captured with only A)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Sign convention: net consumption of A typically implies dA_dt < 0 for A > 0, often enforced by a leading minus sign multiplying nonnegative functions of (t, A).
- Reaction order identification: linear dependence on A suggests first-order; curvature on log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) suggests a power-law A**c.
- Equilibrium approach: terms proportional to (A - c1) indicate relaxation toward a steady concentration c1 (fixed point at A = c1).
- Self-limitation: factors like (c1 - A) introduce a stable upper bound (A approaches c1), common in limited-precursor or inhibition-dominated regimes.
- Time-dependent operating conditions: multiplicative functions of t (e.g., exp(c*t), (c0+c1*t), 1+c*sin(c*t)) indicate nonstationary kinetics such as catalyst decay, programmed feed, or periodic forcing.
- Nonlinear acceleration vs inhibition: superlinear powers (A**c with c>1) imply rate accelerates with A (autocatalysis/chain branching surrogate), while sublinear or saturating fractions A/(A+c) imply diminishing marginal rate at high A.
- Initial-rate offset: an additive constant term c0 in dA_dt can represent background production/consumption independent of A (e.g., feed or leakage), but may create nonphysical behavior if it drives A negative unless balanced by other terms.
- Finite-time blow-up check: strongly superlinear positive feedback (e.g., +c*A**c with c>1) can yield runaway behavior; physical plausibility often requires additional limiting terms or negative feedback.

Structure desc      : Affine-in-A baseline plus an A-scaled decaying exponential in t and an exponential-of-sine in A. The A baseline has c0+c1≈-0.0387, the t-term 0.1388*A*e^{-0.581t} is transient, and the exp(sin) term has moderate nonlinearity (c5=0.329) with amplitude c4=0.309 creating bounded oscillatory modulation in A. For large t, simplifies to ≈ -0.0387A + 0.309*exp(0.329*sin(0.291A+5.776)).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK6)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidate formulas: 199

GT is the fixed function of two variables
\[
f(t,A)= -0.4465879557\,A\,e^{-0.08660230052\,t} \;+\; 0.9910484652\,\sin(\sqrt{A}).
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **(i)** an \(A\cdot e^{kt}\) term with \(k=-0.0866...\) and coefficient \(-0.4466...\), **and** **(ii)** a \(\sin(\sqrt{A})\) term with coefficient \(0.9910...\). In particular, the \(t\)-dependence and \(A\)-dependence are separable exactly as above, and the sine part depends on \(\sqrt{A}\), not on \(A\) linearly, not on \(\log A\), not inside an exponential, etc.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether its functional forms can be tuned (by choosing its free constants) to equal the GT **for all** \(t,A\).

---

### 1. \(A(c0+c1)+A c2 e^{c3 t}+c4 e^{c5\sin(Ac6+c7)}\)
Has an \(A e^{c3 t}\) term (good for the decaying exponential part), but the other non-exponential term is \(e^{\sin(\text{linear in }A)}\), not \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). You cannot choose constants to turn \(e^{c5\sin(\cdot)}\) into \(\sin(\sqrt A)\) for all \(A\). **No.**

### 2. \(A c0 e^{c1 t}\sin(c2 t+c3)+ A^{c4} c5 e^{c6 t}\)
Contains either oscillatory-in-\(t\) factor \(\sin(c2 t+c3)\) or a pure \(A^{c4}e^{c6 t}\). GT has no sinusoid in \(t\). Setting the oscillatory term to 0 leaves only \(A^{c4}e^{c6 t}\), which cannot also produce \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

### 3. \(A(c0+c1)+A c2 e^{c3 t}+A^{c4}c5\)
Only algebraic powers of \(A\), no \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

### 4. \(A(c0+c1)+A c2 e^{c3 t}+ \frac{A^{c4}c5}{A^{c4}+c6}\)
Rational/power in \(A\), no \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

### 5. \(A c0 + \frac{A c1}{A+c2}+ A^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\)
No \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

### 6. \(A c0 + \frac{A c1}{A c2+c3}+ \frac{A^{c4}c5}{A^{c4}+c6}+ \frac{c7}{A c2+c3}\)
No \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

### 7. \(A c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}\sin(c3 t+c4)+ A^{c5}c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Has \(t\)-sinusoid unless killed; then no \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

### 8. \(A c0 + \frac{A^{c1}c2}{A^{c1}+c3}+ c4 e^{c5 t}\)
Only exponential in \(t\) without factor \(A\) (unless forced via other terms, but those are \(A\)-only). No \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

### 9. \(A c0 + c1 e^{c2\sin(Ac3+c4 t+c5)} + c6\sin(Ac7+c8)\)
Sine term is \(\sin(\text{linear in }A)\), not \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). Also the exponential term couples \(A\) and \(t\) inside \(\sin(\cdot)\), unlike GT’s separable \(A e^{kt}\). **No.**

### 10. \(A c0 + \frac{A^{c1}c2}{A^{c1}+c3}+ c4 t^{c5} e^{A c6}\)
No \(\sin(\sqrt A)\). **No.**

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK6)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_m*sin(sqrt(A))
Candidates evaluated: 199
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []



I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.4466*A*exp(-0.08660*t) + 0.9910*sin(sqrt(A))`

This has two terms:
1. A term proportional to `A*exp(-0.08660*t)` — a product of A and a decaying exponential in t
2. A term proportional to `sin(sqrt(A))` — a sine of square root of A (no t dependence)

The key basis functions are:
- `A*exp(c*t)` (exponential decay in t, linear in A)
- `sin(sqrt(A))` (sine of square root of A, no t dependence)

Let me systematically check which candidates can produce both of these basis functions.

**Critical observations:**
- `sin(sqrt(A))` is a very specific nonlinear function. It cannot be represented by polynomials in A, `A^c`, `log(A)`, `A/(A+c)`, `exp(A)`, or similar.
- The t-dependence is purely through `exp(c*t)`, not `sin(t)`, `log(t)`, `t^c`, etc.

Let me scan for candidates that could potentially contain both `sin(sqrt(A))` and `A*exp(c*t)`:

For `sin(sqrt(A))` to appear, I need either:
- An explicit `sin(...)` term where the argument can be `sqrt(A)` = `A^0.5`
- An `exp(c*sin(...))` term where I can set c=0 won't work (gives constant)

Let me look for candidates with `sin(A*c + ...)` where the argument could become `sqrt(A)` — but `A*c` is linear in A, not `sqrt(A)`. So `sin(A*c3 + c4)` cannot equal `sin(sqrt(A))`.

What about `exp(c*sin(A*c3 + c4))`? Setting c=0 gives a constant, not `sin(sqrt(A))`.

What about `A^c1 * c2`? If c1=0.5, this gives `c2*sqrt(A)`, not `sin(sqrt(A))`.

What about `A^c1 * c2 / (A^c1 + c3)`? This is a rational function of `A^c1`, which is a sigmoid-like function, not `sin(sqrt(A))`.

What about `log(c*exp(A^c * c) + 1)`? This is a softplus-like function, not sine.

What about `c*sin(c*log(A*c + 1) + c)`? Candidate 171: `A*c0 + c1*sin(c2*log(A*c3 + 1) + c4)`. The argument is `c2*log(A*c3+1) + c4`. For this to equal `sqrt(A)`, we'd need `c2*log(A*c3+1) = sqrt(A)`, which is impossible for all A.

What about `sin(A*c + c*t + c)`? The argument `A*c + c*t` is linear in A, not `sqrt(A)`.

**Candidate 114:** `A*c0 + A**c1*c2 + c3*sin(A*c4 + c5*log(c6*exp(c7*t) + 1) + c8)`
The sine argument is `A*c4 + c5*log(c6*exp(c7*t) + 1) + c8`. Setting c4=0, this becomes `c5*log(c6*exp(c7*t)+1) + c8`, which has no A dependence inside sine. Can't get `sin(sqrt(A))`.

None of the candidates contain `sin(sqrt(A))` or any mechanism to produce it. The sine arguments are always linear in A (like `A*c`) or involve t, never `sqrt(A)` or `A^0.5`.

After carefully checking all 199 candidates, **none** can produce the `sin(sqrt(A))` term that appears in the GT.
